<div id="review_186713833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186713833" />
    <a title="Johnny Atomic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4537764-johnny-atomic"><img alt="Johnny Atomic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311181529p2/4537764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186713833?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johnny Atomic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johnny Atomic" href="/user/show/4537764-johnny-atomic">Johnny Atomic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186713833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1028745811135584429">Love. Hate.<br/><br/>Some people love this book more than Halloween, kittens and Disney World combined. They see it as emotionally charged, creative and raw.<br/><br/>Others see it as a schizophrenic mess that could have more than half it's pages removed and, only then, be laudable as a very mediocre novella.<br/><br/>Like many things that have a huge following, both parties are correct. I loved the book and thus overlooked its flaws, which are glaring.<br/><br/>If the secondary character of Crow fell off the earth and was eaten by Gr</span>
  <span id="freeText1028745811135584429" style="display:none">Love. Hate.<br /><br />Some people love this book more than Halloween, kittens and Disney World combined. They see it as emotionally charged, creative and raw.<br /><br />Others see it as a schizophrenic mess that could have more than half it's pages removed and, only then, be laudable as a very mediocre novella.<br /><br />Like many things that have a huge following, both parties are correct. I loved the book and thus overlooked its flaws, which are glaring.<br /><br />If the secondary character of Crow fell off the earth and was eaten by Great Cthulhu, I could not be happier. Apparently nobody told John, that having a bunch of "Hero" characters tends to mess up a simple plot. More than one protagonist is usually workable. But two, genuine, capitol "H" Heroes just wastes time and annoys people. I choked through the secondary plot because I cared what happened to Felix.<br /><br />The combat scenes were repetitive, but that was on purpose. So I can't help anyone there. If you didn't find it effective, then it wasn't. You're still right and the fans still liked it.<br /><br />Almost everybody agrees that the ending rocks, even the detractors.<br /><br />In terms of comparison to the other two oft mentioned members of the "Holy Trinity" of power armor stories: "Starship Troopers" and "Forever War", I think it holds up just fine.<br /><br />Most negative reviewers will hold one of the other two books up as a Holy Grail of combat sci-fi. That just comes off as pretentious to me. "Starship Troopers" was not that well written, and "Forever War" falls into a weird pretension more often than I would have liked. I enjoyed all three and none of them are Shakespeare...<br /><br />Armor is fun and dark and has a lot of holes in it. But overall it is my favorite "power armor" novel of all time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1028745811135584429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_350793972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350793972" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350793972?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/10660214-armor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=military-science-fiction">military-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=used-books">used-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350793972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1401756987326478962">Roll together Joe Haldeman’s <i>The Forever War</i>, Heinlein’s <i>Starship Troopers</i> and Arnold’s Terminator, and you get the influences on <i>Armor</i>. It must have been part of the zeitgeist of the mid-1980s, as Card’s <i>Ender’s Game</i> was published right around the same time. The suit of armor is its own character, which binds the two bits of the story together. At first, we follow the exploits of semi-superman Felix, as he battles the Ants, an insect-like interstellar enemy of Earth (very like the Buggers of <i>En</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1401756987326478962" style="display:none">Roll together Joe Haldeman’s <i>The Forever War</i>, Heinlein’s <i>Starship Troopers</i> and Arnold’s Terminator, and you get the influences on <i>Armor</i>. It must have been part of the zeitgeist of the mid-1980s, as Card’s <i>Ender’s Game</i> was published right around the same time. The suit of armor is its own character, which binds the two bits of the story together. At first, we follow the exploits of semi-superman Felix, as he battles the Ants, an insect-like interstellar enemy of Earth (very like the Buggers of <i>Ender’s Game</i>). Eventually, we see space-pirate Jack Crow acquire the suit of armor and explore it’s stored memories with two scientists on a world that he is supposed to be infiltrating.<br /><br />It was engaging, although I found the Jack Crow sections to be a bit opaque in meaning. Why did the author switch to his point of view? I’m unsure. And I found long unbroken stretches of text, where it was difficult to find a reasonable place to leave a bookmark, pausing places if you will. <br /><br />All in all, military science fiction isn’t really my thing, although I appreciate the things that it can say about society. <br /><br />Book 202 of my science fiction &amp; fantasy reading project.<br /></span>

<div id="review_137220379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137220379" />
    <a title="Jason Fischer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4628594-jason-fischer"><img alt="Jason Fischer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442498314p2/4628594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137220379?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Fischer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Fischer" href="/user/show/4628594-jason-fischer">Jason Fischer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137220379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2376020924558206280">I've gotta say, I came into this book with high expectations. It started off brilliantly, with a great Starship Troopers feel....and then not only did the wheels fall off, the whole plot caught on fire and crashed into a kitten orphanage. No-one survived.<br/><br/>The Jack Crow plot-arc was AWFUL, waffling, pointless. GET ON WITH IT. There were points where the editing was abysmal, and I'm not just talking about the occasional typo. I'm talking about bits where paragraphs collided and partially repeated t</span>
  <span id="freeText2376020924558206280" style="display:none">I've gotta say, I came into this book with high expectations. It started off brilliantly, with a great Starship Troopers feel....and then not only did the wheels fall off, the whole plot caught on fire and crashed into a kitten orphanage. No-one survived.<br /><br />The Jack Crow plot-arc was AWFUL, waffling, pointless. GET ON WITH IT. There were points where the editing was abysmal, and I'm not just talking about the occasional typo. I'm talking about bits where paragraphs collided and partially repeated themselves, and I'm mystified as to how this sort of thing got by an editor. At one point, a doctor checks on a person who fainted, and their diagnosis? "this person is emotionally and intellectually exhausted." HOW DO YOU MEASURE THAT? There are points where the Jack Crow arc is logjammed with pointless cipher characters and about halfway through I had to lob this book into the rarest of categories....DID NOT FINISH.<br /><br />How is this book considered awesome and canonical? HOW?</span>
  <a data-text-id="2376020924558206280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_60685528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60685528" />
    <a title="Nagrom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2447349-nagrom"><img alt="Nagrom" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60685528?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nagrom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nagrom" href="/user/show/2447349-nagrom">Nagrom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone. Military Personnel. Sci-Fi and Military Sci-Fi fans.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60685528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18422750450743199468">Many have compared this book, often unfavorably, to Starship Troopers. Some going as far as to call it a rip off of Starship Troopers. I take a different perspective...<br/>In an interview Steakley has actually said that he was inspired by Starship Troopers when he wrote Armor, and took many ideas for his book from Heinlein's. Not in an effort to steal, but as a compliment - Borrowing a scenario he loved and using it to explore a different idea.<br/>Starship Troopers is an exploration of citizenship, duty</span>
  <span id="freeText18422750450743199468" style="display:none">Many have compared this book, often unfavorably, to Starship Troopers. Some going as far as to call it a rip off of Starship Troopers. I take a different perspective...<br />In an interview Steakley has actually said that he was inspired by Starship Troopers when he wrote Armor, and took many ideas for his book from Heinlein's. Not in an effort to steal, but as a compliment - Borrowing a scenario he loved and using it to explore a different idea.<br />Starship Troopers is an exploration of citizenship, duty, and patriotism in human terms.<br />Armor is an exploration of war and will - The human drive, and the resiliency of the human animal under the most extreme of circumstances. This exploration is primarily through the experiences of Felix, and the reactions of his observers, Jack Crow and company.<br />Felix is a soldier. A very good soldier. Too good. He cannot, will not, be defeated. Every battle, every fight, every amount of seemingly insurmountable difficulty he encounters, he champions. Suffering, being injured, but never being destroyed, and continually throwing himself and being thrown back into the fray. Against an endless, unstoppable, enemy, a race of giant sentient ants, who never stops coming. For all his victories, Felix' reality remains the same: The Antwar. A conflict, unexplained even to its fighters, on a desolate hellhole world: The planet Banshee, a barren desert, with subzero temperatures and screaming winds.<br />Felix' experience is shown through the recording devices inside his powered combat armor, which has come to be in the possession of a group of scientists, and Armor's secondary protagonist Jack Crow. As Crow and others become more and more sucked into Felix' world of despair and terror, made only more terrifying by his unstoppable will to never quit, their own problems only grow. Their own quiet place in space is becoming unstable, local forces and an enemy of Jack Crow's past coming together for a final conflict that forces them out of Felix' memories, and into a war of their own.<br /><br />This book succeeds not for the writing - Which is either brilliant literary eccentricity, or just not that well crafted depending on your perspective - or even for the plot. It succeeds and a story of the human will. The machine, the monster, that lies within every man, and how he can choose to champion it, or let it destroy him. And of what a man of character and will is capable of doing with that monster - That "Engine". <br /><br />This is one of the few books I visit over and over again. I have favorite parts and passages, which provide comfort, strength and reinforcement in times of need. <br />I also cannot keep a copy of this book on my shelves, as I am constantly giving them to people who need to read it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18422750450743199468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13154033541795341401">I had this one written down on a little piece of paper I keep in my wallet after reading a gushing review at another website. For months I kept an eye open for it until finally it had been re-issued as a classic.<br/>It was OK but I'd hardly call it a classic. It does have its moments. Damn, the more I think about it</span>
  <span id="freeText13154033541795341401" style="display:none">I had this one written down on a little piece of paper I keep in my wallet after reading a gushing review at another website. For months I kept an eye open for it until finally it had been re-issued as a classic.<br />It was OK but I'd hardly call it a classic. It does have its moments. While battle scenes begin to bore me after 10 pages, I have to admit these ones were pretty intense. And, yeah, the armor was pretty wild.<br />And, yeah, I did begin to feel for the poor guy. Damn, the more I think about it, the more I start to like it.<br />So why was I so anxious to finish it and move on to something else? I guess Steakley's prose just doesn't quite click with me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5803129918066876026">Solid military scifi focusing on a single young Scout who manages to be sole survivor from his unit in more than one attack. Divides into sections, with the seemingly abrupt change of protagonist (and date) from Felix to Jack Crow taking awhile to re-connect with Felix's story.</span>

<div id="review_171757385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171757385" />
    <a title="Alain DeWitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2743688-alain-dewitt"><img alt="Alain DeWitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300045282p2/2743688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171757385?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alain DeWitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alain DeWitt" href="/user/show/2743688-alain-dewitt">Alain DeWitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2743688-alain-dewitt?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171757385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16439279338172632025">There's no easy way to put this: this book was a HUGE disappointment. Several people had recommended it to me in the past. One colleague even went so far as to say it was better than 'Starship Troopers'. As Vincent Vega says in 'Pulp Fiction', 'That's a bold statement.' And as Lee Corso (if he were a junkie stopping by to buy smack from Lance) might have retorted, 'Not so fast, my friend!'<br/><br/>There are so many things wrong with this book. Where to begin?<br/><br/>First, there is almost no character developmen</span>
  <span id="freeText16439279338172632025" style="display:none">There's no easy way to put this: this book was a HUGE disappointment. Several people had recommended it to me in the past. One colleague even went so far as to say it was better than 'Starship Troopers'. As Vincent Vega says in 'Pulp Fiction', 'That's a bold statement.' And as Lee Corso (if he were a junkie stopping by to buy smack from Lance) might have retorted, 'Not so fast, my friend!'<br /><br />There are so many things wrong with this book. Where to begin?<br /><br />First, there is almost no character development for either of the main characters, Felix and Jack Crow. It's a bit understandable in the case of Felix since he has a secret that is revealed at the end of the book. Jack Crow is a mildly interesting character. He has a heavy reputation that clearly all the other characters in the book are aware of but we, the reader, learn almost nothing of. So, in the end, I found him a disappointment.<br /><br />Second is the plotting. Put simply, it's horrid. This is really two novellas that have almost no relationship to one another, connected by the loosest of threads. It's like 'Full Metal Jacket' that is really two movies connected by Pvt. Joker. Only the connection between these two stories is even more tenuous.<br /><br />Third is the action. Much of the action involves Felix in combat in the title armor on the planet Banshee. It's a promising premise poorly executed. All of the action is repetitive as can be. Felix kicks an ant. Felix punches an ant. Felix rips an ant's head off. Repeat ad infinitum.<br /><br />Fourth - and this relates to the action - is the writing style. It's uninteresting and repetitive. The premise of fighting the ants and human troopers in powered armor is highly derivative of Heinlein's 'Starship Troopers'. We don't learn anything about the ants or why mankind is fighting them. They are nothing more than mindless, giant ants and are depicted as such. If that is the case, then how in the heck did they manage to master space flight and attack Earth? It just doesn't follow.<br /><br />Then there is the depiction of the fighting done by Felix. Felix is scared. Felix is tired. Felix is petrified. Felix is exhausted. Felix is horrified. Felix is fatigued. We get it. Use some of those paragraphs to give us a slightly bigger picture view of the fighting or the world or the culture of space-faring mankind or the ants or something. Yes, I get that Felix isn't supposed to have a view of the big picture, but that doesn't mean that Steakley can't give the reader a larger perspective.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16439279338172632025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15958541880072180762">This often-overlooked military Sci-Fi novel has some of the best pulse-pounding, page-turning SF shoot-em-up action you will ever read. Regrettably, the entire book doesn't hold up to the quality of those scenes. Dialogue gets a bit trite at times, especially the internal monologue of Felix who revels in melodrama, female characters exist mostly to hop into bed with the closest male characters, and the pace is clunky with two storylines that could have been more skillfully interwoven. But overal</span>
  <span id="freeText15958541880072180762" style="display:none">This often-overlooked military Sci-Fi novel has some of the best pulse-pounding, page-turning SF shoot-em-up action you will ever read. Regrettably, the entire book doesn't hold up to the quality of those scenes. Dialogue gets a bit trite at times, especially the internal monologue of Felix who revels in melodrama, female characters exist mostly to hop into bed with the closest male characters, and the pace is clunky with two storylines that could have been more skillfully interwoven. But overall it's worth reading for those who enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17214.Starship_Troopers" title="Starship Troopers by Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Starship Troopers</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21611.The_Forever_War__The_Forever_War___1_" title="The Forever War (The Forever War, #1) by Joe Haldeman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forever War</a>. </span>

<div id="review_298013190" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298013190" />
    <a title="Ric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2990467-ric"><img alt="Ric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514254938p2/2990467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298013190?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ric" href="/user/show/2990467-ric">Ric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/9780285-armor">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298013190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17647928532080821074">Re-read August 2020: Still wallops a punch even with a vague recollection from the first read decades back. Despite the sorrowful undertow, this book does have an optimistic premise, that there is life beyond tragedy, one that can find joy in the human experience under any circumstance. <br/><br/>--------------<br/>A military action book with heart and compassion. Who would've <b>thunk</b>! Initially, it seemed like one of those SF ideas that goes thus:<br/><p>
  <i>Young boy with nothing to do observes an anthill. Puts a stick</i></p></span>
  <span id="freeText17647928532080821074" style="display:none">Re-read August 2020: Still wallops a punch even with a vague recollection from the first read decades back. Despite the sorrowful undertow, this book does have an optimistic premise, that there is life beyond tragedy, one that can find joy in the human experience under any circumstance. <br /><br />--------------<br />A military action book with heart and compassion. Who would've <b>thunk</b>! Initially, it seemed like one of those SF ideas that goes thus:<br /><p>
  <i>Young boy with nothing to do observes an anthill. Puts a stick through one of the small holes and lo and behold ants stream out. Pokes more holes and soon has the whole hive agitated. Imagines he is fighting a battle with the ants. Ants discover him and start coming up his legs. That night, while scratching the itchy welts on his feet, thinks, "What if <b>I</b> wrote a science fiction story about my battle with the ants?"</i>
</p><p>But ... there is more to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/102327.Armor" title="Armor by John Steakley" rel="nofollow noopener">Armor</a>. It does take its bursts of adrenaline from the action segments, but it also takes time for introspection and examining the feelings of the characters, though not to the extent of being touchy-feely. The book is like its main characters, hard on the outside but emotionally tender.</p><p><i>Personal impressions:</i> There is a melancholy in the writing, and an anger at specific aspects of life, ostensibly associated with the military. I read in one of the reviews here on Goodreads (<i>love the earnest folks of this online community!</i>) that the author passed away before a sequel was completed. Maybe this is autobiographical? Not with respect to the Ant War, but in terms of the experiences of the two main characters. If you don't watch out, the underlying sadness could get to you.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="17647928532080821074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_133264495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133264495" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3971007-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461261523p2/3971007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133264495?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/3971007-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133264495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11648592726792474151">There are parts of this book that are fantastic, and parts that are a little slow, but overall it was a great action sci-fi. It reminded me a little of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8935689.Consider_Phlebas__Culture___1_' title='Consider Phlebas (Culture, #1) by Iain M. Banks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Consider Phlebas</a> (mainly the character of Jack Crow) as well as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21611.The_Forever_War__The_Forever_War___1_' title='The Forever War (The Forever War, #1) by Joe Haldeman' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forever War</a> (though it seems like every sci-fi soldier book I read reminds me of that one). The parts with Felix were just awesome - I couldn't put it down. The parts with Jack though... I kind of wonder what the point was. Clearly, when you get to the end the reason for his stor</span>
  <span id="freeText11648592726792474151" style="display:none">There are parts of this book that are fantastic, and parts that are a little slow, but overall it was a great action sci-fi. It reminded me a little of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8935689.Consider_Phlebas__Culture___1_" title="Consider Phlebas (Culture, #1) by Iain M. Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Consider Phlebas</a> (mainly the character of Jack Crow) as well as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21611.The_Forever_War__The_Forever_War___1_" title="The Forever War (The Forever War, #1) by Joe Haldeman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forever War</a> (though it seems like every sci-fi soldier book I read reminds me of that one). The parts with Felix were just awesome - I couldn't put it down. The parts with Jack though... I kind of wonder what the point was. Clearly, when you get to the end the reason for his story is provided, but I guess I just didn't like Jack, and his story paled in comparison to Felix's - I found I was a little bored. The novel did tie everything together - the reason for Felix's "Engine" and his skills made sense, as did his rationale for joining the Ant War. And there were parts that were just heart-wrenching; the section with Forest, for one. I also enjoyed the gender-neutral aspects of the novel with regards to the female fighters (not once are the women treated as less-able simply for being women) and the scientists on Sanction. Sometimes I wish people in real life would take a cue from these sci-fi books written years ago. <br /><br />The concept of the suits themselves, though pervasive in our culture right now (i.e. Halo and other games or movies), was still unique and intriguing. Though it might be just my weird fetish for body armour.<br /><br />Great novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11648592726792474151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_222213811" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222213811" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/545336-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329191662p2/545336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222213811?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/545336-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mike by: </span>
      aggie_mike2003@yahoo.com
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=xcharity-2012">xcharity-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222213811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11123401677070586841">Oh man, if only the whole book was a good as the last 100 pages, it would get 5 Stars not just 3. Alas, there are two or three great stories here, but none are fully fleshed out. The first story is about Felix, a survior of uncounted "drops" on Banshee, home of the enemy "Ants". Felix is the ultimate soldier in his <b>Armor</b>, wreaking havoc on the hordes of enemy 1,000# "ants" that attack any military landing on the planet.<br/><br/>The second story revolves around Jack Crow, a famous brigand and scoundrel, a</span>
  <span id="freeText11123401677070586841" style="display:none">Oh man, if only the whole book was a good as the last 100 pages, it would get 5 Stars not just 3. Alas, there are two or three great stories here, but none are fully fleshed out. The first story is about Felix, a survior of uncounted "drops" on Banshee, home of the enemy "Ants". Felix is the ultimate soldier in his <b>Armor</b>, wreaking havoc on the hordes of enemy 1,000# "ants" that attack any military landing on the planet.<br /><br />The second story revolves around Jack Crow, a famous brigand and scoundrel, and his bid for freedom and a ship to carry him to wherever. The Armor of the title connects them but I can't tell you without a major spoiler foul.<br /><br />I think a third story could have been fashioned out of the colony and the underground freedom fighters. Some interesting characters there, unfortunately never given a chance to shine. <br /><br />In the end, the "Antwar" was boring. The enemy reminded me of the stupid threads in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Pern___1_" title="Dragonflight (Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a>, unthinking, stupid enemies. The controlling intelligence for the ants was never addressed or even why we wanted to fight on the planet. The action is good military stuff but against a pointless foe. And the "Fleet" personnel are portrayed beyond dumb, just not believable.<br /><br />The Jack Crow story is more fun but so disjointed and just lacking background in key areas. The denouement is nice and leaves you wanting so much more. A decent read but not the slam dunk I was expecting. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11123401677070586841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17223444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17223444" />
    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/963507-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204588251p2/963507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17223444?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/963507-dan">Dan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/963507-dan?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17223444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15703423788345162686">One of my all-time favorite sci-fi's from an author who has not done anything nearly as well since.<br/><br/>A soldier in a horrific and seemingly unwinnable war loses his identity and self within his armor. Willing to die, he never does. Meanwhile (in the narrative which traverses between the stories), decades after the war, a pirate/crook and a pair of scientists discover a piece of armor floating in an abandoned spaceship. They begin the process of reviewing the armor's files by basically reliving the </span>
  <span id="freeText15703423788345162686" style="display:none">One of my all-time favorite sci-fi's from an author who has not done anything nearly as well since.<br /><br />A soldier in a horrific and seemingly unwinnable war loses his identity and self within his armor. Willing to die, he never does. Meanwhile (in the narrative which traverses between the stories), decades after the war, a pirate/crook and a pair of scientists discover a piece of armor floating in an abandoned spaceship. They begin the process of reviewing the armor's files by basically reliving the experiences of the soldier who had worn it.<br /><br />Often, sci-fi stories seem to be entirely about an idea, but this one is about the human experience in many ways. It delves into questions of identity and deals with high-minded issues like honor, nihilism, and hope while having some very very intense battle scenes as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15703423788345162686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_651418457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/651418457" />
    <a title="Daniel Roy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5368477-daniel-roy"><img alt="Daniel Roy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513163643p2/5368477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/651418457?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Roy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Roy" href="/user/show/5368477-daniel-roy">Daniel Roy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/10660214-armor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer651418457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6743194801867973809">Perhaps it's the comparisons to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17214.Starship_Troopers' title='Starship Troopers by Robert A. Heinlein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Starship Troopers</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21611.The_Forever_War__The_Forever_War___1_' title='The Forever War (The Forever War, #1) by Joe Haldeman' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forever War</a> that ruined this book for me. I went in expecting a thoughtful military SF novel dealing with war and trauma, and although there was some of that, overall the story left me dissatisfied.<br/><br/>A big part of the problem is that the story does a sharp narrative turn about a third into the book. We go from a gritty, straightforward military SF story following Felix, to the first person narration of Jack Crow, a dashing pirate who attemp</span>
  <span id="freeText6743194801867973809" style="display:none">Perhaps it's the comparisons to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17214.Starship_Troopers" title="Starship Troopers by Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Starship Troopers</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21611.The_Forever_War__The_Forever_War___1_" title="The Forever War (The Forever War, #1) by Joe Haldeman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forever War</a> that ruined this book for me. I went in expecting a thoughtful military SF novel dealing with war and trauma, and although there was some of that, overall the story left me dissatisfied.<br /><br />A big part of the problem is that the story does a sharp narrative turn about a third into the book. We go from a gritty, straightforward military SF story following Felix, to the first person narration of Jack Crow, a dashing pirate who attempts to infiltrate a scientific outpost on the orders of a pirate and deserter. It was jarring to say the least, and as a result I never connected with Jack Crow. Oh, he's well-written and interesting, sure, but he's not the protagonist I wanted to read about. Besides, I found the characters he dealt with to be flat and uninteresting.<br /><br />And so, by the time we learn more about Felix, I had stopped caring for the story altogether. Perhaps my reading experience would have been different if I had known about the book's structure going in, but regardless, there's just something makeshift about the book, like the author wrote about Felix then got bored with the subject matter halfway through.<br /><br />Felix's psychology was interesting, and I enjoyed reading the first third as he adjusts to the infernal environment of Banshee and the Antwar. Unfortunately, by the end of the novel he's not the everyman soldier anymore, and instead he's some kind of super-soldier survivor whose psyche is unique and unprecedented. That, in my opinion, weakened the story immensely.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Armor</i> suffers from comparisons to the likes of <i>The Forever War</i>, which is a work of much greater subtlety and purpose. There are some good ideas in here, but not enough, in my opinion, to save a disjointed book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6743194801867973809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_75646241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75646241" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1801612-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75646241?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/1801612-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75646241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8935968962070045999">I have given ARMOR ***** stars because it is one of the most realistic and graphically written novels about war, hands-down! <br/><br/>ARMOR is a story of a mysterious guy named Felix who joints the Fleet Navy to escape a painful and terrible past. It's during basic training that he's found to have unique warrior skills; a remarkable adaptability to combat situations and an incredible, almost superhuman will to live. He's made a Scout and given the standard, fully armored battle suit which is complete wit</span>
  <span id="freeText8935968962070045999" style="display:none">I have given ARMOR ***** stars because it is one of the most realistic and graphically written novels about war, hands-down! <br /><br />ARMOR is a story of a mysterious guy named Felix who joints the Fleet Navy to escape a painful and terrible past. It's during basic training that he's found to have unique warrior skills; a remarkable adaptability to combat situations and an incredible, almost superhuman will to live. He's made a Scout and given the standard, fully armored battle suit which is complete with the latest computer controlled technology that provides him with the most up impressive firepower of any soldier in the known universe.<br /><br />He and his fellow warriors are going to need all of that weaponry! Mankind has gone to war with an alien race so lethal, they engender fear even by the mention of their earthly description, Ants. On a savagely hostile desert world, where the air is poisonous and rivers of acid flow, millions of these huge, four-armed killing machines breed every single day with one hive-like goal, the complete destruction of the human race. This nightmarish planet is called Banshee and that is where Felix and thousands of his comrades are deployed.<br /><br />This is one of my most favorite sci-fi military novels ever read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8935968962070045999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NgJj0sYuIJUBOmlRbHKEak+NlsB+u7MzXS8ho+Br8vyAhvoEv0SnOo3+qubRmMPyzkqCbIpZjYW1E9GzAvno6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QNZ4Cju3CTRTD69e83jOzS3hwMCT9LmvlzDwbrxrSw72UuHcQt2Om9/LbOlOkolVrCbUbGcWhxl/DAB+XvlRGQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17568124131395601502">John Steakley, born 1951 in Cleburne, Texas was best known for his science fiction writing. He wrote two major novels, Armor (1984) and Vampire$ (1991), the latter of which became the basis for John Carpenter's Vampires movie. He also wrote several short stories in the sci-fi and fantasy genres. Not a prolific writer, he lived most of his life in Texas, aside from brief spells in South America and</span>
  <span id="freeText17568124131395601502" style="display:none">John Steakley, born 1951 in Cleburne, Texas was best known for his science fiction writing. He wrote two major novels, Armor (1984) and Vampire$ (1991), the latter of which became the basis for John Carpenter's Vampires movie. He also wrote several short stories in the sci-fi and fantasy genres. Not a prolific writer, he lived most of his life in Texas, aside from brief spells in South America and Hollywood in his youth. After a long illness, novelist John Steakley passed away at his home in McKinney, Texas.</span>

But basically, that's the worst reason I can think of for killing. 'That its the right thing to do'. You kill out of outrage or fury or to keep from dying or something like it, that's fine. Hell, kill them rather than bother with them - or be bothered by them. But if you're killing them because 'its the right thing to do', its only the right thing because you've done so many wrong things up until then to make that spot. It's not the right thing to do.
